Kundarakudi Temple-Pandyas, RR Inscriptions..

by rajpandyan_73 on Wed Feb 01, 2006 4:39 pm

Hi team,

Inspite of job pressures, I got a chance to visit my hometown
Karaikudi during the recent holidays. On a day to visit Kundarakudi
temple, I am surprised to know that beside the hilltop, at the ground
level there is a temple is maintained by ASI where a lot of
inscriptions belonging to Pandyas, Rajaraja are there.(Infact, I am
ashamed that I don't this information till then, though I've lived
nearby)

The ASI guard Balakumar was mentioning that Nalini Madam and
Dr.Kalaikovan have read those inscriptions and collected details on
them.

Beautiful Kuduvari Koil it is.. Precious Stone sculptures..

Any team members can throw some more light on this temple site..??

Of course, SP sir, any chance of visiting this temple? If feasible,
I'd love to accomdate..

With regards,
Raj.
rajpandyan_73

Kundarakudi Temple-Pandyas, RR Inscriptions..

by seshadrigokul on Wed Feb 01, 2006 5:39 pm

Dear Raj

A very detailed study of kundrakkudi temples were undertaken by RMHRC /
Dr.Kalaikkovan. It is available in varalaaru magazine published by the
centre.

I myself have visited kundrakkudi several years back - and like you
said - bothered to visit only the hilltop temple.

Kundrakudi carries the legacy of pandiyan sculptors - like keezhcheval
patti, thirukkolakkudi, thiruparamkundram and vettuvan koil.

I studied in karaikudi and am well familiar with the chettinadu area.

Do you know that pillaiyarpatti is one of the earliest surviving
temples of tamilnadu ? It goes back to 3rd century !!!

Rgds
G
seshadrigokul

Kundarakudi Temple-Pandyas, RR Inscriptions..

by ramachandran.mahadevan on Wed Feb 01, 2006 5:45 pm

Raj,

KunRaikudi is a great Pandya Cave temple. We have had the fortune of visiting it with Dr. Kalaikkovan and Dr. Nalini. Their work at ThirukOLakudi caveand kunRakkudi cave has been published in the "varalaaru journal (not varalaaru.com). They can be obtained by contacting Dr.Kalaikkovan.

We were novices when we visited the temple (not that we are experts now, but we posessed 0% knowledge then and we have 0.1% knowledge now) and hence could appreciate the temple only at a miniscule level. I had written abt. that trip to kamal and Gokul. The travelogue is below. You would need TSCII fonts to read the same. A edited version can be read here:http://www.maraththadi.com/article.asp?id=1789

regards,
Ram.

Hi team,

Inspite of job pressures, I got a chance to visit my hometown
Karaikudi during the recent holidays. On a day to visit Kundarakudi
temple, I am surprised to know that beside the hilltop, at the ground
level there is a temple is maintained by ASI where a lot of
inscriptions belonging to Pandyas, Rajaraja are there.(Infact, I am
ashamed that I don't this information till then, though I've lived
nearby)

The ASI guard Balakumar was mentioning that Nalini Madam and
Dr.Kalaikovan have read those inscriptions and collected details on
them.

Beautiful Kuduvari Koil it is.. Precious Stone sculptures..

Any team members can throw some more light on this temple site..??

Of course, SP sir, any chance of visiting this temple? If feasible,
I'd love to accomdate..

With regards,
Raj.

not sure!!)

BTW, G, what supports that it belongs to 3rd century? Is it in the
same name of Pillayarpatti or Marudheeswaram? (the temple may be
actually siva temple - Marudheeswarar - Kusalaambal, and at some
point I think Pillayar might got famous.. )

Interesting to know more..

--- Inponniyinselvan@yahoogroups.com, "S.Gokul"
wrote:
Dear Raj

A very detailed study of kundrakkudi temples were undertaken by
RMHRC /
Dr.Kalaikkovan. It is available in varalaaru magazine published by
the
centre.

I myself have visited kundrakkudi several years back - and like you
said - bothered to visit only the hilltop temple.

Kundrakudi carries the legacy of pandiyan sculptors - like
keezhcheval
patti, thirukkolakkudi, thiruparamkundram and vettuvan koil.

I studied in karaikudi and am well familiar with the chettinadu
area.

Do you know that pillaiyarpatti is one of the earliest surviving
temples of tamilnadu ? It goes back to 3rd century !!!

Kundarakudi Temple-Pandyas, RR Inscriptions..

by jaybee555 on Fri Feb 03, 2006 8:05 am

--- Inponniyinselvan@yahoogroups.com, "Raj" wrote:
Dear Gokul,

Pillayarpatti dating 3rd Century...??? Interesting.. I am in a wrong
impression first that it belogs to Narashima Pallava period..Then
somebody mentioned that it belongs to Pandyas..(is it Venkat sir..?
not sure!!)

There are more than 200 postings relating to KunRakkudi, PiLLaiyArpatti,
and DEsi Vinayagar in the Archives of Agathiyar. Must be more. I can only
remember about 200 off-hand.

The Archives have been made into a website called 'Agathiyar 40000'.
It is also known as 'Treasure House of Agathiyar'.
There are 38000 plus postings in the archives. Hence the name.
We have converted all the Tamil postings into Unicode from TSCII.
We are still having some glitches in searching in Tamil. English is OK.

The pioneer of research about DEsi Vinayagar was Saa.Ganesan. He was
known
as 'Nadamaadum Kamban' or 'Karaikudi Kamban'.
Dr.A.V.Jeyachandrun and I did some research before 1972.
Dr.AVJ made a press release about the date of PiLLaiyarpatti and also
the identification of a group of statues, in the Hindu, Indian Express,
Dinamani and Dinamalar in 1972.

PiLLaiyarpatti was part of my research concerning the 'AruviyUr
NagaraththAr'
and 'AruviyUR Discovery', and also PirAnmalai.





BTW, G, what supports that it belongs to 3rd century? Is it in the
same name of Pillayarpatti or Marudheeswaram?

The Siva in KunRakudi is known as 'ThEnARRIsar'. KunRakkudi is known
as 'ThiruKunRakkudi'. It predates ThEvarm times.

There is a Tamil Brahmi inscription in KunRakkudi. I forgot the words.
In PiLLaiyArpatti, the Brahmi inscription reads ' 'erukkaattuuru kOn
peruparaNan'.



(the temple may be
actually siva temple - Marudheeswarar - Kusalaambal, and at some
point I think Pillayar might got famous.. )


At the sides of the DEsi Vinayagar alias KaRpaka Vinayagar alias
Maragatha Vinayagar as PiLLaiyarPatti PiLLaiyar is known, is flanked
by shrines to Siva and Vishnu.
Nearby is the new temple dedicated to Marudheeswarar which has been
built upon the site of the older temple of the same deity.
Marudhangudi was a township which existed along with ILaiyARRanggudi,
Rajanarayanapuram, etc., when the Nagarathars established their colonies
in Chettinadu.
So much so for now.

Regards

JayBee





Interesting to know more..

With regards,
Raj.
(PS: Studied in KKDI?.. Where and when? I did from ACCET).

(the temple may be
actually siva temple - Marudheeswarar - Kusalaambal, and at some

At the sides of the DEsi Vinayagar alias KaRpaka Vinayagar alias
Maragatha Vinayagar as PiLLaiyarPatti PiLLaiyar is known, is flanked
by shrines to Siva and Vishnu.

I forgot to mention that Siva and Vishnu are in the
form of Sankaranarayana which is one of the sixteen murthi-bEdha
of Siva.
The sculpture is one of the finest that could be seen
of Sankaranarayana. On the right side would be seen Nandhi.
Garuda is on the left side.
I will try to get the photo and scan it and send.
It should be noted that the Desi Vinayakar sannidhi faces
the north. The Sankarnarayana also faces north.
On the western wall, there is another shrine facing east.
This is the Siva known as 'Thiruviingaikkudi MahadEvar',
otherwise known as 'Thiruviisar', 'Thiruviinggaikkudi Naayanaar',
'Marudhanggudiyaana Raasanaaraayanapuraththu udaiyaar', and
'Thiruviinggiichuramudaiya Naayanaar'.
There is also a Lingodhbhava on the souther wall, around
the corner from Thiruviisar.
All these are found inside the kudaivarai.
Thiruviisar is different from Marudhiisar or 'Marudhanggudi
aayanaar' who occupies a newer temple.
Managed to get my folder on PiLLaiyarpatti and
ThirukkunRakkudi.

Regards

JayBee

Kundarakudi Temple-Pandyas, RR Inscriptions..

by seshadrigokul on Fri Feb 03, 2006 7:00 pm

Dear all

Dr.Jaybee's email raised interesting thoughts in my mind. Shankara
naarayana form seems to be a very early form of worship - which is a
surprise to me. I was of the impression that this was an integration
effort initiated at a later time. I was wrong.

I always believed that thiruppathi could have been a form of
shankaranaarayana - based on nammazhvar's "Thazh sadaiyum neel mudiym
on mazhuvum sakkaramum - soozh aravum ponnanum thondrumal...." a very
picturisque description of shankara naarayana.

Rgds
Gokul.S
seshadrigokul

Raj,

KunRaikudi is a great Pandya Cave temple. We have had the fortune
of visiting it with Dr. Kalaikkovan and Dr. Nalini. Their work at
ThirukOLakudi cave and kunRakkudi cave has been published in
the "varalaaru journal (not varalaaru.com). They can be obtained by
contacting Dr.Kalaikkovan.
We were novices when we visited the temple (not that we are
experts now, but we posessed 0% knowledge then and we have 0.1%
knowledge now) and hence could appreciate the temple only at a
miniscule level. I had written abt. that trip to kamal and Gokul.
The travelogue is below. You would need TSCII fonts to read the
same. A edited version can be read here:
http://www.maraththadi.com/article.asp?id=1789
regards,
Ram.

Dear Saminathan/Raj,

Varalaaru jornal is an annual/bi-annual (depending on editor's convenience)run by Dr. M. Rajamanikkanar Centre for Historical Research. It can be obtained by contacting Dr.Kalaikkovan. Here are the contacts:

Dr. M. Rajamanikkanar Centre for
Historical Research
C-87, 10th Cross,
Thillai Nagar west,
Trichirapalli - 620018
Ph: 0431 2740302 (res)
0431 2766581 (off)

The magazine can be obtained by sending a draft in favor of the centre. Pls. contact Dr.Kalaikkovan for the charges that may include the shipment.

Varalaaru.com is a e-magazine of history, where the contents may not contain 100% research. In its present format the magazine is more of a primer forserious research. Needless to say Dr.Kalaikkovan and Dr.Nalini are among the chief contrubutors and act as guides for the rest of the crew in the editorial board.

-- Ram

convenience) run by Dr. M. Rajamanikkanar Centre for Historical
Research. It can be obtained by contacting Dr.Kalaikkovan. Here are
the contacts:
Dr. M. Rajamanikkanar Centre for
Historical Research
C-87, 10th Cross,
Thillai Nagar west,
Trichirapalli - 620018
Ph: 0431 2740302 (res)
0431 2766581 (off)

The magazine can be obtained by sending a draft in favor of the
centre. Pls. contact Dr.Kalaikkovan for the charges that may include
the shipment.
Varalaaru.com is a e-magazine of history, where the contents may
not contain 100% research. In its present format the magazine is
more of a primer for serious research. Needless to say
Dr.Kalaikkovan and Dr.Nalini are among the chief contrubutors and
act as guides for the rest of the crew in the editorial board.
